If you're using them to cut your hair, or the hair of someone else, take your time, keep the top, flat portion of the blades flush with the person's scalp (to minimize cuts), and be very careful around the ears. Second, for men that wear do-it-youself, clean-shaved heads, these clippers are not a good alternative to shaving your head with razors. Try an electric razor (like Norelco) instead, and then clean up the straggler hairs with a razor. Otherwise, as I said, be very careful!

  369. I went through a lot of obstacles to purchase these clippers,but I'm glad that I did so. I started balding at 18(now 23) and despise constantly using a razor or mediocre clippers, to shave my head every week. These clippers are robust and compact, something that I have been actively searching for, for a while.<br /><br />About the product:<br /><br />The power cord is thick, about 1/3 or 1/4 inch in diameter. The housing is made out of what seems to be a high quality plastic, which is a beautiful burgundy on the front side of the clippers and black on the back. The housing seems like it will protect the internal components for the life of the clipper as long as you don't slam it on the bathroom floor. The on/off switch being small, and at the tapered end of the clippers makes for easy one handed operation. The cutter blade is super sharp and is perfectly aligned(at least on the two models that I received). The comb blade is adjustable, but not by a simple plastic pivot, which I think is a great addition that adds to the quality of these clippers. To adjust the clippers, you just have to unscrew a Phillips screw under the side of the the comb blade and side the the comb blade on a metal rail to your desired position.<br /><br />How the product performs:<br /><br />The feel in the hand is great. I'm a 5'8 male and have medium glove size hands. Not too heavy but you can definitely feel the weight. I have only used this set of clippers a few times since I have just received them not long ago. With that said they have outperformed my expectations. The motor is superior to all others that I have used. The blades cut right through my hair without any hitches. The actual shave is closer than any other clipper that I have ever used. It's not as close as a razor, but does give some stiff competition. I only have to pass over each section of my head once to get a clean shave, even though I do two just to be safe. With other clippers(cheaper and not commercial ones) I have to run them over the same spot multiple times just to get a mediocre cut. In some of the other reviews people complain about being cut by these clippers, but I have not experienced any cuts or scrapes on my head at all. The clippers do vibrate a lot compared to my other clippers, but it is not terrible, and it hasn't been a problem. I hope these clippers will last a while because they are a pleasure to use, and because of the close shave I can go longer periods without having to use them.<br /><br />I would definitely recommend these clippers to any person who is looking for a great, high quality set of clippers for a great value that will give a close shave, or anyone wants to attach guards to these and cut longer hair as well(as I assume they would do a great job).

  606. I'm quite impressed with the 5 Star Clipper. The old cutting guides from my other Wahl fit perfectly. The clipper is relatively small and has a nice heavy duty feeling to it. I'm not sure why, but some people have complained about the weight. For comparisons's sake, the clipper and cord weigh 18.125 oz, and while it has heft, it's definitely not too heavy. I also posted some pics of the clipper next to a tape measure. When operating normally the clippers aren't loud, and sound about the same as any barber's clipper you've ever heard. If your clippers chatter when you plug them in the first time, adjust the plastic screw in the side until it stops. The instructions spell out everything. The blades are sharp enough that they cut 1/8&#34; hair cleanly down to almost nothing with no stragglers or clumps. For me, the clipper leaves about 1/64&#34; fuzz on my noggin, and that's plenty close enough for a shave. Seems many folks complain about the clipper gouging their scalp. Well, on first use I had absolutely no issues. The clipper glides smoothly and does not gouge at all. Keep the bottom blade taper somewhat parallel with your noggin and you will have no issues. If someone's having problems I can only assume they are incapable of operation, or the clipper is not adjusted correctly. There are a couple of things. Closely inspect the cutter head and you may find a few teeth from the top blade (the one doing the cutting) are sticking past the bottom blade. This tip came from another reviewer here, and it seems to be a quality control issue. Also, you may find the top blade is too close or sticking past the bottom blade. Simply loosen the screws holding the bottom blade and slide it forward a little, and re-tighten. Wahl recommends leaving the tip of the top blade (does the actual cutting) 1/32&#34;-1/16&#34; back from the tip of the bottom blade (the one fixed with two screws). Again, this is all in the instructions. ***UPDATE 03-21-2016*** Been using this thing the past few years. Just ordered a replacement blade, and that sucker is sharp. Clipper is good as new.

  655. I've been cutting my own hair since junior year of college. I always use the clipper without any attachment to get the closest shave possible. I was at first nervous from reading both on Amazon and elsewhere the reports of people cutting themselves with the very sharp, close blades. I nevertheless bought a pair, and the same day tried it out. I was that first day very cautious and slow, and I still spent much less time cutting my hair. But the cut was the closest I'd ever gotten--either from a barber or myself. Even though I still don't enjoy cutting my hair, the Wahl 8110 gives such a close, even cut that it is relatively painless.<br /><br />Well, not entirely painless. As I've become more confident about using the clipper I've begun to press into my scalp a bit harder. And I suffered a really nasty nick this last time for my carelessness. I suppose that's the cost of a very close clipper. I agree with other reviewers who've shared that keeping the blade flat against the scalp minimizes the potential for nicks. To this I'd add that refraining from pressing the clipper down even moderately onto the flesh also decreases the chance for nicks. Seems intuitive, but after years of having to weigh down other clippers with sailboat anvils to get them somewhat close to the scalp, I'm having to learn how to cut hair while lightly gliding the clipper across the scalp.<br /><br />Overall I'm happy with the 8110, and will likely replace it with its analogwhen this one wears out. An added bonus, the machine feels well built, gives the impression it will last a while--unlike my other clippers which averaged about 8 months each. Nice job, Wahl.

  949. Definitely not one of the Wahl clippers you normally find at the mall or a department store. I had two of those and while I liked them, they're in a different class.<br /><br />My barber has a razor with interchangeable blade heads and the finest is five-ought (00000), which gets close enough that no one can actually see the stubble left. This clipper has a 6-ought blade, meaning 000000, the closest cut you can possibly get with a clipper, and it's very easy to get bitten if you're not careful about your angle of attack. My scalp gets some red stripes that take a day to subside if I get lazy and raise it up towards vertical to get right down to the skin on the first pass, it's been bad enough that I actually peeled like a sunburn one weekend. The first time you use this clipper should be on the beginning of a full weekend when you don't have plans in case you get a burn like that. It did not make me break out at all, though, but I think that has more to do with keeping your tools clean.<br /><br />That said, this is a great clipper for when you want to be able to get that shaved finish without the effort. For smooth skin, it just works, and it'll do your head in ten minutes without rushing, which I think is necessity considering how much effort it actually takes to have the ultimate in low-effort hair-dos.<br /><br />You must, must, MUST coat the entire blade with WD-40 after rinsing it in the sink. This was recommended to me by my barber, and it solves all the problems with maintenance and longevity other users seem to have. AS WD-40 is, well, WD-40, I bought a gallon in a metal can eight years ago that came in a pack with a quality pump spray designed for it and now the pump lives under the bathroom sink where I can always find it. I rest the clipper on an old kitchen sponge for storage and don't any issues with the WD making a mess.
